=245  \\$aLes Psaumes de David, mis en vers françois, & les cantiques sacrés
=250  \\$aRev. ed.
=260  \\$aBasel$bImhof$c1774
=300  \\$a472-180 pages$bgilded edges
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aIncluding one loose page with ms. notes about psalmbooks, probably written by D.W.L. Milo, on the backside of a concert flyer.
=500  \\$aThe translation of the psalms go back to John Calvin (1509-1564). In 1562 a collection of psalms (known as the Genevan Psalms) was published, suitable to be sung during the service. Calvin had started rhyming in Strasbourg himself. Back in Geneva, he handed this work over to Clément Marot and Beza, while he asked Guillaume Franc, Louis Bourgeois and Maitre Pierre to compose the music. Calvin's zeal in making a collection of psalms arose from his wish to use the Bible alone, also for the hymn. Later editions were edited by members of the 'Compagnie des pasteurs de l'église protestante de Genève'. 
=534  \\$aOriginally published in 1698
=561  \\$aEx libris D.W.L. Milo (stamp)

=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aDorat, Claude-Joseph$d1734-1780$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q361456$98577
=245  \\$aLes Prôneurs, ou Le Tartuffe littéraire,$bComédie en trois actes, en vers.
=260  \\$aParis$bDelalain$c1777
=300  \\$aviii-87 pages$b4 insterted engravings
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aA lively satire of the people in Julie de Lespinasse's society, i.e. the philosophical party. Dorat kept it in his portfolio for several years without being able to have it performed. The philosophers, who were not spared, used the powerful men of their party to prevent the play from being performed. The main character of the play is D'Alembert who, under the name of "Callidès", plays the role of leader of the advocates. The scene in which he initiates a young follower into the mysteries of the order is very pleasant. In this play we find some portraits drawn with a rather vigorous brush, among others, those of Palissot and Clément de Dijon, of whom Dorat had reason to complain; of the former, because he had portrayed him in a less than advantageous manner in his Dunciade; of the latter, because he had made a bitter criticism of his poem De la déclamation.
=500  \\$amotto by Voltaire on the frontispiece: "Le Philosophe est seul, & l'Imposteur fait Secte."

=500  \\$aBenjamin Hederich (1675-1748) was a German encyclopedia and textbook author. From 1702 he worked as a teacher, first at the school in Kloster Berge, later as rector in Grossenhain. In his spare time he wrote introductions to numerous sciences, as well as dictionaries and textbooks in Greek and Latin. His guidance on the noblest historical sciences includes the fields of chronology, genealogy, heraldry, numismatics and diplomacy; without using this term, he put together a canon of auxiliary sciences that has survived almost unchanged to this day.

=500  \\$aJuliana de Lannoy (1738–1782), was an artist and poet from the Northern Netherlands.
She is known for her wit and commentary on women in society, and often wrote about strong women, most notably Kenau Simonsdochter Hasselaer, who featured in her play about the siege of Haarlem in 1770 that she dedicated to William V, Prince of Orange. She is known for plays, poems, watercolours, works on silk.

=100  \\$aVolkmann, Johann Jacob$d1732-1803$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q113563$98583
=245  \\$aHistorisch-kritische Nachrichten von Italien $p1-3/3
=260  \\$aLeipzig$bFritsch$c1770-1
=300  \\$a3 vols. (xxvi-682-[8] + viii-872 + [viii]-846-[42] pages)$bengraved frontispiece, red edges, engraved title vignet
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aOne of the most influential German art books of the 18th century. Spread over three volumes, it systematically provides information about churches, palaces, art collections, musical life, but also about the history of all important Italian cities from Turin to Naples. As a guide to historical Italy, the 'Volkmann' accompanied Goethe, Karl Philipp Moritz, Johann Gottfried Seume and many other Germans on their travels. Goethe, for example, wrote to Charlotte von Stein in 1787: " I am now reading the good, dry Volckmanns zweyten Theil to note what I have not yet seen." (Kippenberg)
=500  \\$a3 identical engraved title vignets depicting 2 little boys holding a map of Italy
=500  \\$aFrontispiece engraving by Christian Gottlieb Geyser (1742-1803)
=500  \\$amanuscript notes on front matter of vol. 1 and 2
=500  \\$apensil markings throughout

Aus den neuesten französischen und englischen Reisebeschreibungen und aus eignen Anmerkungen zusammengetragen.

=245  \\$aNützlicher und brauchbarer Vorrath von allerhand Poetischen Redens-Arten, Beywörtern, Beschreibungen, scharffsinnigen Gedancken und Ausdrückungen
=260  \\$aLeipzig$bGroß$c1725
=300  \\$a[xvi]-112-864 pages$btitle page in red and black ink
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$acommonplace book
=500  \\$aJohan Georg Hamann was a German librettist and writer, a cousin of his famous nephew of the same name J. G. Hamann (1730-1788). He became a private tutor and was active as a publicist, contributing to Gottsched's periodical 'Die vernünftigen Tadlerinnen'. 
=500  \\$aHe wrote for Georg Philipp Telemann: the libretto to the opera 'Margaretha, Queen of Castile' (Hamburg 1730), translated Metastasio's recitatives of  Didone abbandonata for 'Der Streit der kindlichen Pflicht, oder, Die Flucht des Aeneas nach Latien' (Hamburg 1731), and the libretto for the opera 'Der Weiseste in Sidon' (Hamburg 1733).
=590  \\$aNebst einer kurtzen Erklärung der mythologischen Nahmen, aus den besten und neuesten deutschen Dichtern zusammen getragen, und der studirenden Jugend zum bequemen Gebrauch an statt eines Poetischen Lexici, mit einer Anweisung zur reinen und wahren Deutschen Dicht-Kunst ans Licht gestellet.

=245  \\$aAdres-Calender der Königl. Preußl. Haupt- und Residentz-Städte Berlin

=300  \\$a[xxviii]-247-[42] pages$btitle page in red and black ink
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aadress book of Berlin in 1764
=500  \\$aThe Berlin address calendars appeared annually between 1704 and 1918 under different titles.
=500  \\$aThe Berlin address calendars list the higher-ranking persons and office holders of the royal Prussian residential cities of Berlin and Potsdam as well as their authorities, administrations and organizations. The address and description of the authorities are listed, as well as the person's name, official title and private address. At the end of each entry is an index of names. From 1878 onwards, information from the neighboring city of Charlottenburg is also included.

=245  \\$aAmusemens philologiques en prose et en vers$bou mélange agréable de diverses pièces, concernant l'histoire des personnes célèbres, les évènemens mémorables & l'histoire naturelle$p3
=260  \\$aHalle$bMaison des Orphelins$c1780

=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aLater edition
=500  \\$aoriginal in 2 vols. , 1749-1750
=500  \\$aChoffin was a scholar and philologist, born in Héricourt (F) on October 2, 1703, died in Halle (D) in January 1773.  He obtained the double position of professor of modern languages at the school of the Orphans and at the university of Halle, and he contributed by his writings and his lessons to spread the use of French in Saxony.
=500  \\$aEditor's emblem depicting sunbeams & cultivated land with saying "illo splendete levabor' and the initials WH, referring to Weisenhaus Halle  (La Maison des Orphelins à Halle). The Latin motto "Illo splendente levabor" (By his splendor I will be exalted) was intended to testify to the godliness of the institution. The sower in the foreground was interpreted by Bible-loving contemporaries as a reference to the Gospel of Mark (4:14): "The sower sows the word." And this was precisely Francke's basic concern: to change the world by means of the word.

=008  220505s1660\\\\||||||||\||||\00|\p\fre\d
=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aGodeau, Antoine$d1605-1672$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q586272$97907
=245  \\$aPoësies chrestiennes
=250  \\$a2nd ed.
=260  \\$aParis$bPetit$c1660
=300  \\$a508 pages$bengraved title page
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aAntoine Godeau was a French bishop, poet and exegete.
=500  \\$aAntoine Godeau (1605-1672) first published the Poësies Chrestiennes in 1633 in the context of the Catholic Reformation which encouraged spiritual revival. This lyric collection is emblematic of his comprehensive poetic and spiritual work. Godeau became the Bishop of Grasse in 1636 and devoted his poetic gifts to enlightening the readers. This new edition is the latest version of the Poësies Chrestiennes (1660), which is pastoral Catholic verse addressed to the socialites of the time. The versatile poet expressed himself in various forms, registers and topics to convey the Christian dogma and the Bible. The content and the purpose of the book fluctuated. The Poësies chrestiennes was thus a field for experimentation : it became Antoine Godeau's laboratory for all his pastoral and lyric work. The poet defined the principles of a poetry which was based on the conciliation of divine enthusiasm and reason, a poetry where grace and beauty met. The paraphrase of the Scriptures was an opportunity to explore the conciliation of Parnassus and Calvary, as well as the specificity of a classical poetic language in the making, endowing it with gentleness and clarity. Poetry appeared to be the ideal way to instill Christian truths in the heart of the faithful. The religious conversion of secular literary rhetoric prepared the layman to hear the poet-preacher’s vigorous speech. Antoine Godeau tempered his Augustinian anthropology by promoting a life both wordly and pious, in chime with the ideal of Christian “honnêteté”. The poet spiritualized profane aesthetics, which showed his unrelenting desire to adapt his conversion discourse to a public eager to be edified by the “delectare”.
=504  \\$aCamille Venner, Édition critique des "Poësies chrestiennes" (1660) d'Antoine Godeau précédée d'une introduction sur la pastorale lyrique et catholique de cet auteur, These, Université de Lorraine, 2018
https://hal.univ-lorraine.fr/tel-01752385

=100  \\$aSaavedra Fajardo, Diego de$d1584-1648$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2715411$98592
=245  \\$aIdea de un principe politico christiano, representada en cien empresas
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bJanssonius$c1664
=300  \\$a[xxxv]-983 pages
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aDiego de Saavedra Fajardo (1584-1648) was a Spanish diplomat and man of letters.

=500  \\$ain 1640 Saavedra published the anti-Machiavellian emblem book Empresas Políticas. Idea de un príncipe político cristiano, a hundred short essays about the education of a prince. This work was written primarily for the son of King Philip IV. It passed through a number of editions and was translated in several languages.
=500  \\$aSaavedra's 'Idea de un príncipe político cristiano' was a very erudite work that uses the literary sort of emblem, put by Andrea Alciato with his 'Emblemata' translated in 1549 and that has a mainly moral and philosophical character. His work, however, was mainly inspired by the 'Emblemata política' (1618), by Jakob Bruck Angermunt, being the intention of the author to compose a guide for the suitable political formation of a Christian prince.

=041  \\$alat$afre
=245  \\$aCantus diversi pro Dominicis, festis et feriis per annum
=260  \\$aToulouse$bDouladoure$c1745
=300  \\$a286 pages
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$apages 282-286 include a 'Manière pour bien chanter dans un chœur' (without title page), derived from 'Trois methodes faciles pour apprendre le plein-chant' (1689).
=500  \\$aThis set of three anonymous methods could have been commissioned by Claude Bachelu, a bookseller from Lyon who was worried on several occasions for counterfeiting or for having distributed banned books. Having published numerous works of spirituality and theology, Bachelu brought out in his name a collection of Cantus diversi (1689). Like Parisian colleagues such as La Caille, he doubled this publication with a theoretical counterpart, thus the 'Trois methodes'. Modeled from the easy method designed for the Parisian seminary of Saint-Nicolas du Chardonnet, they then benefited from a long editorial existence since they are found at the end of several other books imitating that of Bachelu, and this until the middle of the 18th century. The 'Three methods' are (partly) included with a new title page and new compositions in the Cantus diversi by Claude Moulu (Lyon, 1700) and by Gaspard Henault (Toulouse, 1745) or, without title page, in the Cantus diversi ex Graduali Romano by Pierre Valfray (Lyon, 1724) and this edition by Joseph Douladure (Toulouse, 1745). (for more information see: https://www.cantus-scholarum.univ-tours.fr/ressources/sources/methodes-faciles-de-plain-chant/trois-methodes-1698/)
=500  \\$ams. scribblings on back matter
=561  \\$aEx libris (?) (blue stamp, with a crown and key)
=590  \\$aEx Graduali Romano. Nova editio, lectior, correctior & auctior. Accedunt Missæ Burdigalensis et Missæ Regales, novem Lectiones Jeremiæ, novaque triplex Methodus Cantus ediscendi

=500  \\$aMoritz von Strachwitz (1822-1847) was a German lyric poet. When traveling in Italy in 1847 he was taken ill in Venice, and died in Vienna. Although he had thus only reached his twenty-fifth year, he revealed a lyric genius of remarkable force and originality. His early death was a great loss to German letters; for he was by far the most promising of the younger lyric poets of his time.

=500  \\$aA picaresque novel, in the style of Le Sage’s Gil Blas. Thibault was governor of Talmont, and this is his only known work. Set in Spain, it deals with the love story of a rogue, facing the galleys. It was enormously popular, being translated into English, German, Iberian, and Castillian. Also published under the title: Histoire comique et galante de Pédrille del Campo.

=100  \\$aBlumauer, Aloys$d1755-1798$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q79087$98614
=245  \\$aVirgil's Aeneis in neun Gesängen
=260  \\$aLeipzig$bKöhler$c1841
=300  \\$a296 pages$b36 plates inserted
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aAloys Blumauer, also known as Alois Blumauer or Johannes Aloysius Blumauer, (1755-1798) was an Austrian poet.
His works, which are chiefly coarse satires on the clergy and on the Jesuits (of which he himself had become a member a year before its dissolution in 1773), enjoyed a wide popularity. He is remembered, however, chiefly for his Abenteuer des frommen Helden Æneas (1784–88; published with introduction and commentary by E. Griesbach, 1872), a coarse travesty on Vergil's Aeneid. Blumauer is also remembered as an acquaintance of Mozart, the lyrics of whose Lied der Freiheit (KV 506, 1786) he penned.

=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$a2 volumes in 1
=500  \\$aThe History of Sevarambians is a utopian novel by Denis Vairasse published in 1675 as The History of the Sevarites or Sevarambi. Originally published in English, it was quickly translated into French and expanded, with parts two and three appearing in 1677 as L’Histoire des Sévarambes. Two further instalments were published in French in 1679. The novel did not appear in its completed form in English until 1738. The novel depicts an ideal world in Australia.

=300  \\$a[xii]-1040-[12] pages$bengraved frontispiece, title page in red and black ink, 28 insterted engraved plates
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aChristian devotional literature
=500  \\$aThe term "Erbauungsliteratur' (edification literature), first mentioned around the 14th century, originally describes popular writings with a religious motivation. Edification literature is not theological literature, as it does not pursue scientific discourses and has no dogmatic intentions. Rather, with the changes of the modern era, there was a focus on inwardness, which stood out through increased piety. It was a guide to a virtuous life that was intended to emotionally edify the mind. 
=500  \\$aJohannes Lassenius (1636-1692) was a German Lutheran theologian and devotional writer of the Baroque period.

=500  \\$aWilhelmus Schortinghuis (1700-1750) was a Dutch Reformed clergyman. He is best known for his book 'Het Inninge Christendom' (1740) and the "vijf nieten" (the five nots): "ik wil niet, ik kan niet, ik weet niet, ik heb niet en ik deug niet" (I don't want to, I can't, I don't know, I don't have and I'm no good), with which he wanted to make clear. that a man could contribute nothing to his salvation. He is regarded as a representative of the late phase of the 'Nadere Reformatie', which is often referred to as Reformed Pietism.

=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aSenault, Jean-François$d1599-1672$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q3165889$98453
=245  \\$aDe l'usage des passions
=260  \\$aParis$bJournel$c1660
=300  \\$alxxii-492 pages$bengraved frontispiece
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aOriginally published in 1641
=500  \\$aA book on the ‘usage’ of emotions by the French Augustinian preacher, Jean-François Senault. He approached the subject of the ‘passions’ from a variety of angles: their uses and dangers, how to moderate them and how a prince should use them. The treatise was often reprinted in different formats and translated into English, German, Italian and Spanish. The work is divided into two parts, the first of which deals with the passions in general and the last with each in particular.
=500  \\$aOf the nature of passions -- Of the disorder of passions -- Of the government of passions -- Of the commerce of passions with vertue and vice -- Of the power that passions have upon the will of man -- Of love and hatred -- Of desire and eschewing -- Of hope and despair -- Of audacity and fear -- Of choler or anger -- Of delight and sorrow.

=100  \\$aFleming, Paul$d1609-1640$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q77418$98650

=500  \\$aPaul Fleming (1609-1640), was a German physician and poet. Fleming is one of the writers now called "the Silesian poets" or "the Silesian school". As a lyricist he stands in the front rank of German poets.
=500  \\$aFleming wrote the hymn in nine stanzas "In allen meinen Taten" on the melody of "Innsbruck, ich muss dich lassen" by Heinrich Isaac, which is contained in several hymnals. Johann Sebastian Bach used the final stanza to close both cantatas Meine Seufzer, meine Tränen (BWV 13) and Sie werden euch in den Bann tun (BWV 44). The complete hymn is the base for Bach's chorale cantata In allen meinen Taten (BWV 97). Already in the 17th century another composer, David Pohle (1624–1695), had set twelve of Fleming's love-songs to music. Johannes Brahms set "Lass dich nur nichts bedauern" as Geistliches Lied, Op. 30.
=500  \\$acontains an engraved title page and a portrait of the author on the frontispiece
=534  \\$aTeutsche Poemata, published posthumously in 1642

=100  \\$aCotolendi, Charles$d16..-1710?$4aut$98651
=245  \\$aRéflexions sur les divers stiles et sur la manière d'écrire, $bou Dissertation sur les œuvres de Monsieur de Saint-Evremont
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bHoogenhuysen$c1700
=300  \\$a[viii]-344-[8] pages
=500  \\$aSieur Dumont, otherwise known as Charles Cotolendi (Barbier), was a lawyer at the parliament of Paris and distinguished literary scholar. Hortense (Ortensia) Mancini was a niece of Cardinal Mazarin, chief minister of France, and a mistress of Charles II, King of England, Scotland, and Ireland. She was the fourth of the five famous Mancini sisters, who, along with two of their female Martinozzi cousins, were known at the court of King Louis XIV of France as the Mazarinettes. With the exception of Marguerite de Valois, Hortense and her sister, Marie Mancini, were the first women in France to put their memoirs into print. Both women were partly motivated by the help that producing a body of evidence would bring to the cause of separation from their abusive husbands.

=100  \\$aTillet, Jean du$cSieur De La Bussière$dca 1500 - 1570$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q3175829$924341
=245  \\$aChronicon de regibus Francorum, a Pharamundo vsque ad Henricum II
=260  \\$aParis$bVascosan$c1548
=300  \\$a167 pages
=500  \\$aChronical of the French Kings, from Faramundus (420) until Henry II (1547)
=500  \\$aLayout in table form divided into 4 columns (3 for dates and one for text)
=500  \\$aJean du Tillet, Sieur de La Bussière (circa 1500-1570), was a jurist and historian and clerk of the Parliament of Paris. Secretary to the king under Henry II, he was gifted with an immense erudition, both legal and historical. He was one of the first historians to write about French history based on archival documents.
=500  \\$aTitle page contains several remarks in ms, in different hands, possibly referring to provenances of the book:
- in red ink: "Tecum habita", a drawing of littel snail and "Joannes Moflinus"
- "Sr Petrus de Manchicourtii bethunij"
- "Ama et Time"
- "Eura et Arte JCarlier"
=500  \\$aThe composer Pierre de Manchicourt (c. 1510 – 5 October 1564) was born in Béthune, 6 hours on foot or 2 on horseback from Arras (France), where he was a choirboy at the cathedral. De Manchicourt worked in Tours from 1539 to 1545. At the time of the publication of "Chronicon", however, in 1548, Henry II had just been king for one year and De Manchicourt had been back on Habsburg territory, in Tournai, for three years.
=500  \\$aThe "tecum habita" (literally translated "live with yourself") written above the name of Joannes Moflinius and the snail was, among others, the motto of the book dealer-printer Ludovicus Cyaneus (or Louis Blaublom) from Ghent, who worked in Paris between 1528 and 1546. Cyaneus, however, had a turtle as its printer's mark, not a snail. The inscription is probably made earlier by Joannes Moflinius, abbot of the abbey of Sint-Winoksbergen, in the period of Charles V and Philip II.  Sint-Winoksbergen is located 60 km coastal from Béthune, near Dunkirk. This abbot corresponded with humanists such as the cathographer Ortellius and the printer Christophel Plantijn.

=100  \\$aCalvin, Jean$d1509-1564$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q37577$95913
=245  \\$aLes Pseaumes de David$bmise en rime Françoise
=260  \\$aParis$aCharenton$bCellier$c1675
=300  \\$a[626]-8-[4] pages$bembossed leather cover, front- and backmatter contains manuscript notes in French and cyphers$epostcard 
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aOriginally published in 1551, the translations of 150 Psalms of David by Clement Marot (1496-1544) as completed by Theodore de Bèze (1519-1605, Calvin's successor as spiritual leader of the Republic of Geneva) were used almost exclusively by the Calvinists (Genevan Psalter). The psalter was the main medium of popular fervour among the Reformed. The Edict of Nantes forbade Reformed worship in towns where the King of France resided and the only town allowed around Paris was Charenton. 
=500  \\$aFollowed by The Form of Ecclesiastical Prayers, The Form of Administering Baptism, The Manner of Celebrating Holy Communion, The Catechism, and Daily Exercise of the Christian.

=100  \\$aDu Roullet, François Louis Gaud Lebland$cMarquis$d1716-1786$4lbt$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q3083494$98660

=260  \\$aParis$bAntoine$c1793
=300  \\$a24 pages
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$a'Iphigénie en Aulide'  is an opera in three acts by Christoph Willibald Gluck, the first work he wrote for the Paris stage. The libretto was based on Jean Racine's tragedy Iphigénie, itself based on the play Iphigenia in Aulis by Euripides. The choreography was by Gaétan Vestris. It was premiered on 19 April 1774 by the Paris Opéra in the second Salle du Palais-Royal and revived in a slightly revised version the following year.

=041  \\$adut
=245  \\$aWetten van het departement der muzyk, in de maatschappy, ter spreuke voerende: Felix Meritis
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bUylenbroek$c1790
=300  \\$a31 pages$bengraved title page
=500  \\$aTitle page engraving (seated Apollo with lyre) after Jacques Kuyper (1761-1808), a Dutch printmaker, painter, draftsman, watercolourist, etcher, musician, and composer. Kuyper became a member of the Felix Meritis artist community.
=500  \\$astatutes of the music department within the Felix Meritis Society
=500  \\$aFelix Meritis ("Happy through Merit") is the name of an intellectual society for Music, Drawing, Physics, Commerce and Literature in Amsterdam, founded in 1776.  In 1788 the new building they built for themselves on the Keizersgracht in Amsterdam opened its doors. Felix Meritis’ oval concert hall was the main music hall in Amsterdam until late into the 19th century and enjoyed a great international reputation. Many famous musicians performed there, including Robert and Clara Schumann, Camille Saint-Saëns, Johannes Brahms and Julius Röntgen. The orchestra of Felix Meritis was regarded as the best of the Netherlands and accompanied many Dutch premieres, directed by conductors such as Johannes Bernardus van Bree. Thus, Beethoven’s Ninth Symphony and Berlioz’s Symphonie fantastique had their Dutch premiere in the concert hall of Felix Meritis. The small hall of the Concertgebouw is a replica of this concert hall.

=100  \\$aChampein, Stanislas$d1753-1830$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q3496656$98675
=245  \\$aOuverture de la Mélomanie.$cArrangée pour le clavecin ou le piano forte avec violon ad libitum
=260  \\$aParis$bBoyer$c1783
=300  \\$a10 pages$bPrinter's Signature stamp on title page
=500  \\$aArranger Charles Fodor was a Dutch composer and harpsichordist. He was the son of soldier Carolus Fodor (and later violinist) and Maria Elizabeth Messemaekcers, who came from a musical family. The brothers Joseph Fodor and Carolus Antonius Fodor also became musicians. Charles Fodor is the least known of the three brothers. He became a music teacher in Paris, made transcriptions of quartets by Pleyel and symphonies by Joseph Haydn. He himself wrote sonatas and variations (including Air de Tonnelier), but a symphony for large orchestra (Symphonie à grand orchester en re) by him is also known. There are also two concertos for harpsichord by him, one of which he performed in Amsterdam in December 1790. His works were mainly published in Paris and Amsterdam. He probably died in Paris in the last 10 years of the 18th century or early 19th century.

=500  \\$aLa double épreuve, ou Colinette à la cour, is a comédie lyrique in three acts written by André Grétry in 1782 to a French libretto by Jean-Baptiste Lourdet de Santerre, based on Charles Simon Favart's Ninette à la cour. It was first performed on 1 January 1782 by the Académie Royale de Musique (Paris Opera) at the Théâtre de la Porte-Saint-Martin, and included choreography by Maximilien Gardel.

=500  \\$a'Alexis et Justine' a comédie lyrique mêlée d’ariettes in deux actes by Dezède on a libretto by Jaques-Marie Boutet de Monvel (1745-1812) premiered in Paris, Opéra-Comique, in 1783

=500  \\$aJohann Franz Metzger, born in Enkenbach in Landkreis Kaiserslautern, baptized December 26, 1729, was a German pianist and composer, from 1785 active in Paris. He was still alive in 1808 and probably died shortly afterwards. Metzger also composed cello sonatas, and dLa Bataille de Fleurus (tone painting for piano which describes the Battle of Fleurus in 1794), which was an important component of the well-known musical process in Uppsala in 1800, a notorious trial against seven academic citizens on the occasion of their "strike" as musicians in the Royal Academic Chapel at a party celebrating Gustav IV Adolf's coronation.

=100  \\$aGarth, John$d1721-1810$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2517501$95352
=245  \\$aA Second Sett of Six Sonatas for the Harpsichord, Piano Forte and Organ, with Accompanyments for two Violins and a Violoncello op. 4
=260  \\$aLondon$bWelcker$c17xx
=300  \\$a25 pages
=500  \\$aKeyboard part only
=500  \\$aGarth, English composer, organised for many decades a concert series, the Durham concerts, in alternate weeks to those organized by his friend Charles Avison in Newcastle, where Garth played the cello. Garth's fame spread and he taught music to leading families in the region, as well as giving organ recitals. Garth is chiefly remembered for his eight-volume edition with English text of The First Fifty Psalms Set to Music by Benedetto Marcello (1757–65), but he also composed a set of cello concertos (op. 1, 1760) and five sets of harpsichord sonatas (opp. 2, 4–7, 1768–82), among other works.

L'Élève qui sera en état de bien exécuter ce qui lui est offert, pourra facilement entreprendre des Sonates: mais pour parvenir a la perfection des doux mains, pour rompre toutes les difficultés il faut se servir de la grande Méthode du Doigté de L. Adam et Lachnith qui fait la suite de cet ouvrage.

=100  \\$aKotschoubey,  Princess Elisabeth Vassilievna $d1821-1897$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q102284079$98702
=245  \\$aOh ! dites-lui. Romance $bchantée par Tamberlick
=260  \\$aMainz$bSchott$c1861
=300  \\$a[1]-3 pages$bEngraved title page
=490  \\$a'Lyre Française'$vno. 783.1070
=500  \\$asong by a female composer, a member of the Ukrainian princely family Kotschoubey. Princess Elisabeth Vassilievna Kotschoubey (née Kotschoubey) (1821-1897) was a well known composer of both Russian and French popular songs in Russia and later in France. She was  married to her third cousin, Prince Leon Viktorovitch Kotschoubey (1810-1890) and they died childless. 
=500  \\$aEnrico Tamberlik (16 March 1820 – 13 March 1889) was an Italian tenor who sang to great acclaim at Europe and America's leading opera venues. He excelled in the heroic roles of the Italian and French repertories and was renowned for his powerful declamation and clarion high notes.
=500  \\$aText writer Larmande was a French state official (chef de bureau au Ministère des Finances), and amateur poet. Known for translating German songs, or rather for providing them with new, French poetry, e.g. in the series Échos d'Allemagne, together with Victor Wilder. His official signature (e.g. on his appointment as Chevalier de la légion d'honneur in 1881) always reads "Ad. Larmande", and his brother Alfred Larmande and sister-in-law Sophie Desargues were professional musicians.
=500  \\$aErnesto Cavallini (1807-74) clarinetist and composer, created in 1862 'Trois Variations sur la romance Oh!Dites-Lui' for Clarinet and orchestra:
https://imslp.org/wiki/3_Variations_sur_la_Romance_Russe_Chante_(Cavallini%2C_Ernesto)

=100  \\$aFontmichel, Hippolyte de$d1799-1874$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1298846$98722
=245  \\$aLe Chevalier de Canolle. Quadrille de contredanses suivi d'une valse, pour le piano, avec accomp. de violon, flûte ou flageolet, ad. libitum
=260  \\$aParis$bLemoine$c1836c
=300  \\$a7-[2] pages$bMusic-seller's stamp at foot of title page
=500  \\$aKeyboard part only
=500  \\$aPrinter's Plate No.1858.H.
=500  \\$aThe 5 numbers of the Quadrille are followed by a Galop;the score contains no 'Valse'.
=500  \\$aDe Fontmichel studied at the Conservatoire de Paris, and in 1822 he received the deuxième Second Grand Prix de Rome for the cantata Geneviève de Brabant. During his stay in Italy he composed two operas: Amadeo il Grande and I due Forzati. After the premiere in 1836 of the comic opera Le Chevalier de Canolle at the Opéra-Comique was a failure, de Fontmichel retired to Grasse, where he devoted himself to farming. Here he composed several opera choruses and an opera on the subject of Hamlet, as well as several romances. He also worked as organist at Grasse Cathedral and the Couvent de la Visitation and composed several religious works.
=500  \\$aHenry Lemoine was a French piano teacher, music publisher, and composer 
=500  \\$aPaper cover belongs to another work in the series of "Contredanses pour le Piano seul arranged and published by Lemoine, as title on the cover reads "à Madem.lle Louise de Golbéry. La Chatte Métamorphosée en femme. Musique de A. Montfort, Premier Quadrille sur des Motifs du Ballet, Composé pour le Piano avec de Violon, Flûte, Flageolet, Basse et Piston ad. lib. Par Henry Lemoine" and has printer's plate No 1966.H. "La Chatte..." is a one-act comic opera from 1858 by Jacques Offenbach, with a libretto by Eugène Scribe and Mélesville.
=500  \\$aContains a complete catalogue of all "Contredanses, Valses et Galops pour le Piano, à deux et quatre mains" published by Lemoine

=500  \\$aThe court oboist Franz Heinrich Ehrenfried worked for 44 years as a recognised musician in his field in the service of the Elector of Mainz or, after its dissolution, in Aschaffenburg. In addition, he played his role as a performing musician in opera, concert life and church music. There are numerous prints of his arrangements, mainly of operas. They offered the middle classes music for reliving stage works, for making music at home and for teaching purposes. The preference for the flute in these prints corresponds to the demand of the time.

=500  \\$aNancy van der Elst was a female composer who taught in Utrecht
=500  \\$atranslation of Paul Gerhardt's Advent song "Wie soll ich dich empfangen"
=500  \\$a"Valet will ich dir geben" is a Lutheran hymn written by Valerius Herberger in 1613. It is a Sterbelied (hymn for the dying). The text was published with two hymn tunes by Melchior Teschner, Zahn Nos. 5403 and 5404a, in 1615. The second of these melodies was used in compositions such as chorale preludes by Johann Sebastian Bach and Max Reger. Bach used single stanzas in vocal works, including his St John Passion.
=500  \\$a"Our God, Our Help in Ages Past" is a hymn by Isaac Watts in 1708 that paraphrases the 90th Psalm of the Book of Psalms. In 1738, John Wesley in his hymnal, Psalms and Hymns, changed the first line of the text from "Our God" to "O God". Both Watts' wording and Wesley's rewording remain in current use.

=500  \\$aJoseph Schad was a German composer and organist. He was a pupil of Louis Schmitt in Frankfurt and for a time was dedicated to giving organ concerts. He established himself as an organist in Morges (CH) , later became a professor at the Conservatory of Genevavand finally settled in Bordeaux where he died. He wrote a large number of fantasies, transcriptions, waltzes, masurques, etc., for piano, vocal melodies and the ballet Franizia.

=100  \\$aMendelssohn-Bartholdy, Felix$d1809-1847$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q46096$94998
=245  \\$aOuverture, Scherzo, Notturno, Hochzeitsmarsch und Intermezzo aus der Musik zu Shakespeare's Sommernachtstraum. Componirt und für das Pianoforte arrangirt op. 61
=260  \\$aRotterdam$bVletter, de$c1844 or later
=300  \\$a40 pages
=500  \\$aKeyboard arrangement by the composer
=500  \\$aAt two separate times, Felix Mendelssohn composed music for William Shakespeare's play A Midsummer Night's Dream (in German Ein Sommernachtstraum). First in 1826, near the start of his career, he wrote a concert overture (Op. 21). Later, in 1842, only a few years before his death, he wrote incidental music (Op. 61) for a production of the play, into which he incorporated the existing overture. The incidental music includes the famous "Wedding March". 
=500  \\$aIn 1844 Mendelssohn arranged three movements for piano solo (Scherzo, Nocturne, Wedding March), which received their first recording by Roberto Prosseda in 2005. Slightly better known is the composer's own arrangement, also made in 1844, of five movements for piano duet (Overture, Scherzo, Intermezzo, Nocturne, Wedding March).

=100  \\$aHöckh, Carl$d1707-1773$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q16859335$98775
=245  \\$aSieben Parthien von zweyen Violinen und Baß
=260  \\$aBerlin$bWinter$c1761
=300  \\$a8-8-8 pages$bengraved cover page $c35x23 cm
=500  \\$aThree parts (violino primo, violino secondo, cembalo) in an engraved paper envelope 
=500  \\$aThe term parthia or partita is by no means to be understood as an unambiguous genre designation; rather, it is used as a kind of collective term. In the present works, it is applied to a trio sonata type with two equal violins and basso continuo, which in turn can be interpreted as a transitional stage to the sonata forms of the burgeoning genres of string trio, piano trio and string quartet.
=500  \\$aHöckh, who was music director at Zerbst on the recommendation of Benda, is considered "one of the founders of the German school of violin playing". He wrote extensively and idiomatically for the instrument, incorporating more advanced techniques than most of his contemporaries. His works include eleven symphonies, seventeen violin concertos, seven partitas, twenty-seven violin sonatas, and thirty-four capricetti.
=500  \\$aEdited by Phillip Schmidt, Ortus Musikverlag, om97
=500  \\$aWhat is curious about the parthias is their unusual number for the 18th century. The Seven Parthias in A, B, C, D, e, F, g are inscribed with Italian tempo markings and are mainly structured in their movement sequence like the modern trio sonata according to the principle fast - slow - fast. Exceptions are the IIIrd Parthia, in which the first movement is heard again after the second, and the IVth Parthia, whose structure is four movements. The final movement here is a tempo di minuetto. Some of the middle movements are in the key of the subdominant, the fourth in the key of the Variant, the sixth in the key of the dominant and the last in the key of the mediant.

=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aNewspaper extract of the Algemeen Handelsblad of 28 mai 1852 (an influential Amsterdam-based liberal daily newspaper published between 1828 and 1970), on the occasion of King Willem III unveiling in 1852 a cast-iron Rembrandt monument designed by Louis Royer on the Amsterdam Botermarkt-square (named Rembrandtplein since 1876). 
=500  \\$a4 pages Biography, ending with poem by Thijm, plus 2 pages text that appeared on the title page of the Newspaper.
=500  \\$aThe biography ends with a long celebrating poem on Rembrandt by J.A. Alberdingk Thijm (1820-1889) titled "Een Harptoon in het Akkoord der Rembrandtshulde"
https://www.dbnl.org/tekst/albe003voor01_01/albe003voor01_01_0016.php

=041  \\$ager
=245  \\$aUnter Allerhöchster Autoriteit Ihro Kön. Maj. zu Dännemark, Norwegen u. Schleswig-Holsteinische Anzeigen 40stes Stück. Montag den 7ten October 1799
=260  \\$as.l.$bs.n.$c1799
=300  \\$a4 pages$bquadruple-folded pages$c42x36c cm
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aThe Schleswig-Holsteinische Anzeigen (SchlHA) is the justice journal of the German federal state of Schleswig-Holstein and at the same time one of the oldest periodicals of the state.
The Schleswig-Holsteinische Anzeigen date back to the time of the duchies of Schleswig and Holstein and have been published since 1750.[1] They are an announcement journal that was published under the same title by both the kings of Denmark and the diverse rulers in Schleswig-Holstein such as the House of Schleswig-Holstein-Gottorf. Today, the publisher is the state's Ministry of Justice, which has left the editorship to the Higher Regional Court of Schleswig. They are divided into a monthly Part A (with the editorial content of a legal journal and contributions on case law in the judicial district of the state's only Higher Regional Court) and a twice-monthly Part B (advertising section and judicial notices). It is therefore an official journal and not an advertising journal.
Part B of the Schleswig-Holstein Advertisements was published twice a month (on the 15th and 30th of a month) in printed form as a justice gazette until the end of 2014. The publication of a written edition of Part B has been dispensed with since 1 January 2015. Therefore, from this date onwards, all issues of Part B (which in future will only be published once on the 30th of a month) will only be made available digitally and free of charge.

=041  \\$adut
=100  \\$aTwist, Albertus van $4aut$98813$d1696-after 1743
=245  \\$aEeuwigduurende liefdes almanak
=260  \\$aCyprus [sic]$bMirtillo$c1721
=300  \\$bengraved frontispiece and title page, leather bound, gild embossed spine, illustrations$a129 pages
=500  \\$acertainly not published in Cyprus
=500  \\$ams. note in the cover revealing Philokalus as the Leiden student Albertus van Twist
=500  \\$afrontispiece engraving depicting "La Naissance de Venus" (3 naked sea Nymphs and Venus)
=500  \\$a"Van Twist, geboren te Hulst in 1699, had zich in 1718 ingeschreven als rechtenstudent te Leiden, waar hij, als we de pamfletten mogen geloven, meer interesse toonde voor lessen in de liefde dan voor colleges. Deze pamfletten zijn blijkbaar geschreven door medestudenten of anderen die getuige waren van de pogingen tot vrijages van Van Twist. De Eeuwigduurende liefdes almanak is dus een sleutelalmanak: achter de fictieve namen in de gedichten gaan echte personen schuil. Daarmee neemt het een unieke positie in temidden van andere Nederlandse almanakken." (kb.nl)
=500  \\$aengravings on frontispiece, title-page and at pages 36, 37-59, 88, 90, 92, 94, and 122
=500  \\$aThe Eeuwigduurende liefdes almanak is one of the first almanacs that is playfully aimed by the writer and publisher who called himself by the antique name Philomúsus Philokaus, admirer of muse and beauty, and thus puts himself in the mythological tradition. This cheeky man placed elements from traditional calendars in amatory/amorous context, like the twelve months of the year of love ‘de twaelf maenden van ‘t jaer der liefde’. Visit is the first month, Hope the fifth, the eight month is called Connection, Regret the eleventh which is followed by Indifference. Also other elements of life and cycles from the year of love are described in the same style as noted above. 
=500  \\$aThe frolic author of this richly illustrated work hid his real identity behind the pseudonyms Philomúsus Philokaus and Philander Mirtillo from Cyprus (which is known as the place where the Roman goddess Venus first touched land after she was born on open sea). Revealing the person behind the almanac became an obsession short after its publication in 1721. Contemporaries tried to light the veil of mystery by spreading pamphlets. This quest ended at the student Albertus van Twist, who aimed to immortalize his impossible love for Johanna Susanna Alensoon. Van Twist, born in Hulst in 1696, registered as a law student in Leiden in 1718. If the pamphlets are right, he paid more interest about lessons of love than the actual law classes. These pamphlets are written by fellow students and other witnesses of Van Twists flirts. The Eeuwigduurende liefdes almanak is thus a key almanac, there are real people behind the fictive names in the poems, which makes this book extraordinary amid other Dutch almanacs. Besides the unusual content, there are more reasons for this book to be very special. Already in the early eighteenth century, right after publishing, this book was rare, concluding by the fact that in later years the author himself bought copies of the book. In the end everything luckily turned out well for the romantic Mister Van Twist. He promoted in 1721, the year of publishing, and moved back to Zeeuws-Vlaanderen, where he got married twice, gave life to a lot of children and finally made it to bailiff.

=100  \\$aTasso, Torquato$d1544-1595$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q168962$94904
=245  \\$aL'Aminte
=260  \\$aThe Hague$bDyk, van$c1681
=300  \\$a[xii]186 pages$bbound in marbled cardboard, manuscript title vignet on spine, inserted illustrations, frontispiece engraving
=500  \\$aOriginally published in 1580
=500  \\$abilingual edition italian-french "Aminta, Comedia / Aminte, Comedie"
=500  \\$aAminta is a play written by Torquato Tasso in 1573, represented during a garden party at the court of Ferrara. Both the actors and the public were noble persons living at the Court, who could understand subtle allusions the poet made to that style of life, in contrast with the life of shepherds, represented in an idyllic way. The text is written in hendecasyllabic and septenary verses; it is divided into five acts. The play has a pastoral theme, and is set in the time of Alexander the Great. The characters are shepherds and nymphs.The story is about Aminta's love for the beautiful nymph Silvia, who does not return his attentions and prefers hunting. She risks rape at the hands of a Satyr but Aminta saves her; however, again she flees from him. Aminta, finding her blood-stained veil, attempts to kill himself. Now Silvia is remorseful, comes back to cry over Aminta's body who is still alive, and the two can happily marry, following the advice that older and wiser friends had been giving them.

=245  \\$aVersuch einer Biographie der Frau Gräfin von Lichtenau
=260  \\$aZurich$aLindau$a[Leipzig]$bs.n.$c1800 [1798]
=300  \\$a[x]-132 pages
=500  \\$aWilhelmine, Gräfin von Lichtenau, born as Wilhelmine En(c)ke, also spelled Encke (1753-1820), was the official mistress of King Frederick William II of Prussia from 1769 until 1797 and was elevated by him into the nobility. She is regarded as politically active and influential in the policy of Prussia during his reign.
=500  \\$aAccording to Waltraud Maierhofer, Wilhelmine was often the subject of satire during her lifetime. This publication, actually published in Leipzig in 1798, seems to be "more a satire against enlightenment ideas than a biography". The author's name, August Wilhelm Baranius, might even be a pseudonym; Waltraud Maierhofer suggests the opera singer Henrietta Baranius (1768-1853). (Source: “Wilhelmine Encke-Ritz-Lichtenau: Writing and Reading the life of a Prussian Royal Mistress." Biography 27, no. 3 (2004): 575–96.)

=500  \\$aMarmontel is a French encyclopaedist, historian, storyteller, novelist, grammarian, poet, playwright and philosopher. He was close to Voltaire in his views and was an opponent of Rousseau. =041  \\$aspa
=100  \\$aVega, Lope de$d1562-1635$4aut$98045
=245  \\$aLaurel de Apolo
=260  \\$aLondon$bLeclere$c1824
=300  \\$axvi-248 pages
=500  \\$aFélix Lope de Vega y Carpio (1562-1635) was a Spanish playwright, poet, and novelist who was a key figure in the Spanish Golden Age (1492–1659) of Baroque literature. Lope de Vega renewed the literary life of Spanish theatre when it became mass culture, and with the playwrights Pedro Calderón de la Barca and Tirso de Molina defined the characteristics of Spanish Baroque theatre with great insight into the human condition. The literary production of Lope de Vega includes 3,000 sonnets, three novels, four novellas, nine epic poems, and approximately 500 stageplays.

=041  \\$aeng
=100  \\$aSwift, Jonathan$d1667-1745$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q41166$97332
=245  \\$aA Tale of a Tub
=250  \\$a9th ed.
=260  \\$aLondon$bBathurst$c1739
=300  \\$a[xxiv]-220 pages$b7 plates inserted, engraved frontispiece
=500  \\$aA 'Tale of a Tub' (see also 11A18 for the French translation) was first published by the Irish clergyman and novelist Jonathan Swift in 1704; it is the first and perhaps most difficult of all his satires. The title is thought to refer to a dissenting priest’s pulpit, and the work is a biting parody on the religious extravagances that Swift perceived among the clergy at the start of the 18th century. The narrative is written using a complex though playful technique of interlinking stories concerning the lives of three brothers, each representing one of the main branches of western Christianity. The edition is particularly noteworthy for the woodcut illustrations that punctuate the text. For example, there is a striking image of a priest reprimanding the congregation down below, with a gallows and theatre shown in the background. The frontispiece also illustrates a whale distracted by a barrel thrown overboard by sailors: an allegory, perhaps, of how the text was designed to draw the attention of political and religious dissenters away from the affairs of the ‘ship’ of state.

=245  \\$aQuestions sur les mathématiques en général
=260  \\$as.l.$cc. 1730 [?]

=500  \\$aoriginates from a Benectine monastery school ?
=500  \\$aEx libris "Dom Antoine Jourdez", the last Benedictine monk of Toul, who wrote a handwritten document, entitled Description of the organ, 1811 and 1813. Attached to this 422-page manuscript is a 47-page Supplement, written in 1882, by Joseph Oury, organist of Toul Cathedral. The organ of the former Saint-Étienne Cathedral of Toul (Meurthe-et-Moselle) seemed to have passed through the Revolution without incident. When the church reopened, the last of the Benedictine monks of Saint-Mansuy, Dom Antoine Jourdez, had the organ restored and assumed the position of organist until September 30, 1828.

=041  \\$adut
=100  \\$aLoosjes, Adriaan Pieterszoon$d1761-1818$4aut$95554
=245  \\$aHet leven van Maurits Lijnslager:$beene Hollandsche familie-geschiedenis uit de zeventiende eeuw
=250  \\$a3rd ed.
=260  \\$aHaarlem$bLoosjes$c1823
=300  \\$a4 vols. (vi-289+263+304+316-[3] pages)
=500  \\$aAdriaan Loosjes (1761-1818) was a Dutch botanist, poet, novelist and publisher. 'Het leven van Maurits Lijnslager', a historical novel, was his best-known book.
=520  \\$aThe writer places the story around the end of the Twelve Year's Truce. Maurits Lijnslager is the son of a merchant from Amsterdam. At the age of eighteen, he must take up his father's office in Livorno. which means he would leave Rotterdam, where he met Maria van Vliet. One of her brothers becomes his traveling companion, although he soon succumbs to the miserable journey. Maurits continues his travels in the company of the Flemish painter Antonie van Dijk and meets the musician Manichetti in Florence. Together they meet the famous Galileo Galilei and Maurits becomes an eyewitness to the capture of this sage. The story also elaborates on his time in Genoa, where he meets Rubens. He declines the offer to settle there for good and travels back to the Netherlands via Switzerland. He returns from his journey with the then still youthful Milton.

=245  \\$aBiographische Skizze von Michael Haydn
=260  \\$aSalzburg$bMayer$c1808
=300  \\$a[iv]-60 pages
=520  \\$aThe most important contemporary source on Johann Michael Haydn's life and work is the Biographical Sketch by Michael Haydn, published two years after his death by the publishing house Mayr'sche Buchhandlung in Salzburg. Published on behalf of his widow and drafted by friends of the composer: Georg Johann Schinn (1768-1833) and Joseph Otter (around 1760-1836) - both his students - as well as Haydn's "most trusted" friend, P. Werigand Rettensteiner (1751-1822) from Michaelbeuern Abbey near Salzburg.
